We have to ensure that the investors who are coming to this country are able to see our rules, regulations and laws as being on par with the rest of the world. That is most important because that is what the investors are searching for. When they are coming to any country, they want to see that the laws are of a standard, which they are used to in their own countries. They must see that the laws are being implemented by people who have knowledge and who will be able to carry out those functions in such way that they will be able to give confidence, and that is what is most important. When the Hon. (Dr.) Nalaka Godahewa gave those figures today, you already saw what a big difference there was from the time our new Government took office last year. The whole market was able to move forward with confidence and with certainty because they were confident that the Government will back those laws as well as regulations to go forward with certainty. So, that is what was lacking and that is what we need to restore. Hon. Speaker, this new law that we have brought forward in Parliament today will provide for the technical aspects of the market as well as the revolutionary new advances that are taking place all over the world to be introduced into our country. The latest developments will be there. We will also be able to ensure that the interest of all stakeholders are safeguarded. There may be a few instances where we need to bring in certain amendments to this Bill and that has been done after consultation with a large number of stakeholders from across the country. They have been able to give us various suggestions as well as certain new ideas that would ensure that this law would be able to be on par with the rest of the world. We are also providing for the central counterparty structures to be introduced and that also will be able to build up confidence in our markets. Sir, the most important part of a capital market is that the laws, the regulations and the rules that we bring in should be able to stimulate the market and not stifle the market. The laws must be of such nature that when these are being implemented that all stakeholders will be attracted, but at the same time they should realize that if they are to be flouting any of these rules and regulations, that would also be addressed very quickly and in a way that it is very transparent as well. Therefore, I want to commend this new Bill to the entire House and we are hoping that all Members of Parliament who are present here today would vote for the passage of this law, so that we will see unanimity as far as this law is concerned. Sir, we are also bringing in the Finance Bill which would provide for one per cent of tax to be paid with regard to the monies that have hitherto not been declared. ගරු කථානායකතුමනි, මෙහිදී සමහර අය මුදල් විශුද්ධිකරණය ගැන පමණක් කථා කරනවා. මේ සියයට එකක බද්ද අපි අය කරන්නේ කළු සල්ලි සුදු කිරීම සඳහා පමණක් බව කියනවා. මෙතැන තිබෙන්නේ එහෙම දෙයක් නොවෙයි, ගරු කථානායකතුමනි. ඇතැම් විට සමහර අය තමන්ගේ ආදායම බදු ගෙවීමට අදාළව ඉදිරිපත් කරලා නැති වෙන්න පුළුවන්. ගරු කථානායකතුමනි, මේ අවස්ථාවේදී අපේ රටේ සමස්ත ආර්ථිකය ගැනත් මා වචන ස්වල්පයක් කථා කළ යුතුයි. අද රුපියල අවප්‍රමාණය වීම ගැන විපක්ෂයේ සමහර මන්ත්‍රීවරුත් කථා කළා. ගරු කථානායකතුමනි, සමහර අවස්ථා වලදී අපි හිතුවාට වඩා රුපියල අවප්‍රමාණය වෙලා තිබෙනවා. එසේ නොවන ලෙස කටයුතු කරන්න අපට සිදු වනවා. ඒක ඉතා වැදගත්. අපි හිතනවා, මහ බැංකුවෙන් වුණත් එවැනි මඟ පෙන්වීමක් - guidance- සමස්ත වෙළෙඳ පොළට ලබා දීලා, රුපියල අවප්‍රමාණය නොවන ආකාරයට කටයුතු කරන්න ශක්තියක් ලබා දිය යුතුයි කියලා. The Central Bank has a responsibility to ensure that there is certain guidance provided to the markets, so that the interest rates and the exchange rates are managed in such a way that that would be most beneficial as far as the country and the economy is concerned. It is a very tough task, Hon. Speaker, to decide on exchange rates. We should not permit only a few people, a few stakeholders, to decide as to what the exchange rates of a country should be. Sometimes, people say that it should be decided only by the traders, by those who are importing as well as exporting. That should not be the case. It should be a very carefully planned effort involving those who are borrowing, those who are lending, those who are remitting money, those who are importing, those who are exporting, all of them and the entire gamut of their transactions should be carefully managed in order to ensure that it would be fair by all stakeholders. That is not very easy to do, but you have do that. So, if you are guided only by one or two stakeholders, invariably you will come up with a wrong answer. So, we must also make an appeal to the importers that they should not import everything they want to because they fear that the rupee would depreciate. They should understand that the Government needs to take certain steps in order to ensure that those imports are staggered in such a way that no one amasses too much inventories as that itself would propel the rupee to depreciate further. At the same time, we must advise the exporters that they should also be conscious of the responsibility of converting their dollars when they come into the country. It should not be a compelling situation. They should be able to convert their foreign exchange into rupees because that is what makes the entire economy run and it is very important for us to recognize that. Sometimes, they may need a little persuasion to do that because in a market where they expect the rupee to depreciate further, there are instances where they would hold on to their dollars, to their foreign exchange expecting to get more as time goes on. That kind of speculation, that kind of expectation can sometimes be quite damaging as far as the economy is concerned. That is why proper guidance is necessary in order to provide for space for all these players to do their businesses as well as to ensure that the country's economy is also taken forward in a realistic as well as a proper manner. Those are issues that we will have to work on. We have to give the support and I believe all that would assist Sri Lanka in its debt management as well. We are also facing this situation as a result of International Sovereign Bonds being excessively issued during the period from 2016 to 2019. We do have a little bit of difficulty to manage that. But at the same time, we need to shift some of that. It is a careful shift that we need to do and for that shift to take place, we can take those decisions. We have already embarked on a programme, Sir, where we are hoping to have non-debt inflows introduced into the country. That is very important so that we do not have debt piling up on further debt. We need to ensure that certain other inflows come into the country by way of foreign exchange, which would ensure that Sri Lanka's overall economy—the external economy—is managed in a way that would be realistic as well as sustainable. To do that, there would be a need to have more and more Foreign Direct Investment and that is why we have concentrated on that. The Colombo Port City Economic Commission Bill was introduced. We also brought in Pharmaceutical Zones and the Hambantota Industrial Zone. All these are designed to bring in new inflows into the country. Through those new inflows, we will be able to address the debt issue by ensuring that some of the inflows we were having only by way of debt are replaced. When debts are to be settled, those will be settled out of the inflows we will get from non-debt inflows. That is the only sustainable way. We do not need someone from outside to come and tell us how to do that. We have a country which has been independent for 73 years. After 73 years, if we still need someone to hold our hand and tell us what we should do with the economy, then I do not think we have really progressed. We have the ability, we have people who understand these issues and we know how to deal with it and that is what is most critical, Sir. So, I want to conclude my speech by saying that we have had tense moments at different times. There are tensions. We understand that also. We are not saying that everything is rosy. But at the same time, we have been able to deal with the situation and that is what is most important. I want to thank the Hon. Minister of Finance for introducing these new laws which will have a great impact on our economy. At the same time, I want to thank all those Hon. Members who provided us with very interesting and important ideas as well as comments, particularly those who are from the Opposition who gave us so many insights. All that is very helpful. We appreciate that. I also commend this law to be passed with the unanimity that it deserves. Thank you very much.
